Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet us quickly have recourse to you, for that your (faculty) of removing (sin) by which you gladden us;waters, bestow upon us progeny.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Let us go to you at once for him to whose house you are hastening; waters,reinvogorate us; faculty of removing sin: kс╣гaya = niv─Бsa, abode;

Aram = pary─Бptim, sufficiency; perhaps arecommendation to be regular in practising ablution

Jamison Brereton

Let us, as your (offspring), go to be fit for him for whose peaceful dwelling you animate
and beget us, o Waters.

Griffith

To you we gladly come for him to whose abode ye send us on;
And, Waters, give us procreant strength.

Geldner

Dem m├╢chten wir euch recht kommen, f├╝r dessen Haus ihr uns erfrischet und neugeb├дret, ihr Gew├дsser.

Grassmann

F├╝r solchen gehn wir euch zur Hand, zu dessen Sitz ihr eilend naht, Ihr Wasser machet kr├дftig uns.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдерд╛рдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╡рдпрдордирд╛рдЧрд╕рдГ рд╡рд┐рдореБрдХреНрддрд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкрд╛рдкрд╛рдГ рддрд╡ рд╡реНрд░рддреЗ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрд╛ рднрд╡реЗрдо ред рдЕрджрд┐рддрдпреЗ рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдбрд┐рддрддреНрд╡рд╛рдп рдЕрджреАрдирддреНрд╡рд╛рдп рд╡рд╛ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореЗрддрд┐ ред рд╣реЗ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдп рдЕрджрд┐рддреЗрдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ - рдЗрддреНрдердордирд╛рдЧрд╕рд╕реНрд╕рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рдпрдорджрд┐рддрдпреЗ рдЕрдирднрд┐рд╢рд╕реНрддрдпреЗ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо ред рдХрд┐рдорд░реНрдердВ? рддрд╡ рд╡реНрд░рддреЗ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрддрд╛рд░реНрдердорд┐рддрд┐ ред рдЕрдирд╛рдЧрд╕ рдЗрддрд┐ рдмрд╣реБрд╡реНрд░реАрд╣реМ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди ‘рдирдЮреНрд╕реБрднреНрдпрд╛рдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рди рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ, рд▓реБрдкреНрддрдорддреНрд╡рд░реНрдереАрдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдирд╛рдЧрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рди рдЗрддрд┐ рее

рд╣реЗ рд╡рд░реБрдг рдЙрддреНрддрдордВ рдЙрддреНрддрдордлрд▓рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рд╣реЗрддреБрдВ рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдХрд░реНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдкрд╛рд╢рдВ рдХрд░реНрдордкрд╛рд╢рдВ рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрдд рдЙрдЪреНрдЫреНрд░рдерд╛рдп рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдореБрддреНрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрдп рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдп рдирд╛рд╢рдп ред рдЕрдзрдордВ рдирд┐рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдлрд▓рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рд╣реЗрддреБрдВ рдЕрдзрдГрдкрддрдирд╣реЗрддреБрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реНрдордкрд╛рд╢рдорд╡рд╢реНрд░рдердп рдЕрдзрд╕реНрддрд╛рджрдкрдХреГрд╖реНрдп рдирд╛рд╢рдп ред рдордзреНрдпрдордВ рдкрд╛рд╢рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд░рдердп рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрд╡рдЩреНрдирд╛рдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рдХреГрд╖реНрдп рдирд╛рд╢рдп ред рдЕрдереИрд╡рдВ рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рдХреГрддреЗ рд╡рдпрдордирд╛рдЧрд╕рдГ рдХреНрд╖рд╛рд▓рд┐рддрд╕рд░реНрд╡рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрдГ рддрд╡ рд╡реНрд░рддреЗ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛рддреНрдордирд┐ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рдЕрджрд┐рддрдпреЗ рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдбрд┐рддреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╛рдп рд╣реЗ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдп рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдорд╛рджрд┐рднреВрдд рдЕрджрд┐рддреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрдкрддреНрдпреЗрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVaruс╣Зa, loosen for me the upper, the middle, the lower band; so, son of Aditi, shall we, through faultlessness in the worship, become freed from siс╣ЗтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Reference to the ligature fastening the head, the feet, and the waist; resulting in loosening from the bonds of sin: an─Бgasaс╕е sy─Бma, may we be sinless

Jamison Brereton

Loosen above the uppermost fetter from us, o Varuс╣Зa, below the lowest, away the midmost.
Then under your commandment, o ─Аditya, we would be without
offense for Aditi [/Guiltlessness].

Griffith

Loosen the bonds, O Varuna, that hold me, loosen the bonds above, between, and under.
So in thy holy law may we made sinless belong to Aditi, O thou Aditya.

Keith

Unloose from us, O Varuna, the highest,
The lowest, the midmost knot;
Then may we, O Aditya [3], in thy rule,
Be guiltless before Aditi.

Geldner

L├╢se die oberste Schlinge von uns, o Varuna, l├╢se die unterste ab, l├╢se die mittlere auf! Dann wollen wir, Sohn der Aditi, in deinem Dienste vor Aditi s├╝ndlos sein.

Grassmann

O Varuna, l├╢s’ ab von uns die Stricke, den untersten, den mittelsten und h├╢chsten, Dann m├╢gen wir in deinem Dienst, Aditja, von Schuld befreit, der Aditi geh├╢ren.

Elizarenkova

(рддрд╡) рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕рдм рдХреЗ рдЧреБрд░реБ рдЖрдкрдХреЗ (рд╡реНрд░рддреЗ) рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд░рдгрд░реВрдкреА рд╡реНрд░рдд рдХреЛ рдХрд░рдХреЗ (рдЕрдирд╛рдЧрд╕рдГ) рдирд┐рд░рдкрд░рд╛рдзреА рд╣реЛрдХреЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдЕрджрд┐рддрдпреЗ) рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдб рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рд░рд╣рд┐рдд рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рдирд┐рдпрдд рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВреерезрелрее

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреА рдЖрдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рдХреЛ рдпрдерд╛рд╡рддреН рдирд┐рддреНрдп рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╣реА рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░ рдФрд░ рд╕рдм рджреБрдГрдЦ рдмрдиреНрдзрдиреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдЕрд▓рдЧ рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВреерезрелреерддреЗрдИрд╕рд╡реЗрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдХрд╣реЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╡рд╛рдпреБ рдЖрджрд┐ рдЕрд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЕрдиреБрдХреВрд▓ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐ рдЖрджрд┐ рдЕрд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдХрд╣рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рдЪреМрдмреАрд╕рд╡реЗрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреА рдЙрдХреНрдд рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд░реБрдг ! рддреНрд╡рдорд╕реНрдорджрдзрдордВ рдордзреНрдпрдордореБрджреБрддреНрддрдордВ рдкрд╛рд╢рдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╢реНрд░рдерд╛рдп рджреВрд░рддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рдпрд╛рдереЗрддреНрдпрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╣реЗ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдп ! рддрд╡ рд╡реНрд░рдд рдЖрдЪрд░рд┐рддреЗ рд╕рддреНрдпрдирд╛рдЧрд╕рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рдпрдорджрд┐рддрдпреЗ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рднрд╡реЗрдореерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдПрд╡рд╛рд░реНрде рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗред

Keith

The bull hath stablished the sky, the atmosphere;
Hath meted the breadth of the earth;
Hath set him in all worlds as king.
All these are Varuna’s ordinances.

рдЕрд╕реНрддреСрднреНрдирд╛реТрджреН рджреНрдпрд╛рдореГреСрд╖реТрднреЛ рдЕреТрдиреНрддрд░рд┐реСрдХреНрд╖реТрдордорд┐реСрдореАрдд рд╡рд░рд┐реТрдорд╛рдгреСрдореНрдкреГрдерд┐реТрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдЖрд╕реАреСрджреТрджреНрд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛реТ рднреБрд╡реСрдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реТрдореНрд░рд╛рдбреНрд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрддреНрддрд╛рдирд┐реТ рд╡рд░реБреСрдгрд╕реНрдп рд╡реНрд░реТрддрд╛рдирд┐

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhatever the offence which we men commit Varuс╣Зa against divine beings, whatever law of yours wemay through ignorance violate, do not you, divine Varuс╣Зa, punish us on account of that iniquity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whatever this deceit that we humans practice against the divine race, o Varuс╣Зa,
if by inattention we have erased your ordinances, do not harm us
because of that guilt, o god.

Griffith

O Varuna, whatever the offence may be which we as men commit against the heavenly host,
When through our want of thought we violate thy laws, punish us not, O God, for that iniquity.

Geldner

Was wir Menschen auch als Frevel am g├╢ttlichen Volke hier begehen, o Varuna, wenn wir unwissentlich deine Gesetze gest├╢rt haben, so sollst du um dieser S├╝nde willen uns nicht zu Schaden bringen, o Gott.

Grassmann

Was wir auch hier, o Varuna, nach Menschen Art f├╝r Unrecht ├╝ben am Geschlecht der Himmlischen, wenn wir verletzten dein Gesetz aus Unverstand, so strafe nicht um diese S├╝nde uns, o Gott.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIf, like gamesters, who cheat at plural y, (we commit offences) knowingly, or (those) of which we know not, do you divine Varuс╣Зa, extricate us from them all, as if from loosened (bonds), so that we may be dear, Varuс╣Зa, to you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

If (we have cheated) as gamblers cheat in a dice game, whether overtly or whether we are unaware,
unbind all these things (so they will be) like loose things, o god. Then would we be dear to you, Varuс╣Зa.

Griffith

If we, as gamesters cheat at play, have cheated, done wrong unwittingly or sinned of purpose,
Cast all these sins away like loosened fetters, and, Varuna let us be thine own beloved.

Geldner

Wenn wir wie Spieler bei dem Spiele betrogen haben, ob wir es gewi├Я wissen, ob nicht, all das l├╢se von uns wie lockere Bande, o Gott! So m├╢gen wir deine Lieblinge sein, o Varuna.

Grassmann

Wenn wir get├дuscht beim Spiel wie falsche Spieler, wenn wir gefehlt, unwissend oder wissend, Was uns verstrickt, das alles l├╢se du uns, Gott Varuna, und wieder sei’n wir lieb dir.

Elizarenkova

рднрдЯреНрдЯрднрд╛рд╕реНрдХрд░-рдЯреАрдХрд╛

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVaruс╣Зa, we deprecate your wrath with prostrations, with sacrifices, with oblations; averter of misfortune, wise and illustrious, be present amongst us, and mitigate the evils we have committed.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

asura = aniс╣гс╣нa-kс╣гepaс╣Зa-┼Ыila, accusative tomed to cast off what is undesired; from seme, to throw

Jamison Brereton

We beg to appease your anger by our acts of reverence, Varuс╣Зa, appease it by our sacrifices and offerings.
Holding sway, o attentive lord and king, you will loosen for us the guilt we have created.

Griffith

With bending down, oblations, sacrifices, O Varuna, we deprecate thine anger:
Wise Asura, thou King of wide dominion, loosen the bonds of sins by us committed.

Keith

Thine anger, O Varuna, would we avert with reverence,
With sacrifices, with oblations
Ruling, O wise Asura, O king,
Do thou unloose the sins we have committed.

Geldner

Wir bitten dir den Groll ab, Varuna, mit Verbeugungen, mit Gebeten, mit Opferspenden. Du, der die Macht hat, einsichtsvoller Asura, K├╢nig, erla├Я uns die getanen S├╝nden!

Grassmann

O Varuna, wir wenden deinen Zorn ab, durch Opfer, durch Gebet, durch Trankesspenden, Der du die Macht hast, weiser, ew’ger K├╢nig, erlasse uns die S├╝nden, die wir thaten.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPraising you with (devout) prayer, I implore you for that (life) which the instrumental tutor of the sacrifice solicits with oblations; Varuс╣Зa, undisdainful, bestow a thought upon us; much-lauded, take not away our existence.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The term, tad─Бyus is supplied in the context of m─Бna ─Бyuс╕е pramoс╣гiс╕е = do not take away our life

Jamison Brereton

Extolling you with my formulation, I implore this of you; with his offerings the sacrificer hopes for this:
Become no longer angry now, Varuс╣Зa! O you of wide fame, do not steal away our lifetime!

Griffith

I ask this of thee with my prayer adoring; thy worshipper craves this with his oblation.
Varuna, stay thou here and be not angry; steal not our life from us, O thou Wide-Ruler.

Geldner

Das erbitte ich, mit beschw├╢rendem Worte freundlich zuredend, das w├╝nscht sich der Opfernde mit seinen Opferspenden: Sei hier ohne Groll, Varuna! Du, dessen Worte weithin gelten, raub uns nicht das Leben!

Grassmann

Dies bitt’ ich dich, verehrend mit Gebeten, und darum wirbt mit Opfertrank der Opfrer: O Varuna, sei bei uns ohne Z├╝rnen, weitherrschender, verk├╝rz nicht unser Leben.

Elizarenkova

May the missile of Rudra spare us,
May the wrath of the brilliant evil worker (pass over us);

O bounteous one, be merciful to our children and descendants.

рд╣реЗ рд░реБрджреНрд░ рд╕реНрддрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорджреНрд╡рдЪрд╕рд╛ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрдорд╛рдиреЛ рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рдЬрд░рдгрд╢реАрд▓реЗ рджрд┐рдиреЗ рджрд┐рдиреЗ рдХреНрд╖реАрдпрдорд╛рдгреЗрд╜рд╕реНрдордЪреНрдЫрд░реАрд░реЗ рдореГрдб рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рдХреБрд░реБред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorify the renowned Rudra, riding in his car, ever youthful, destructive, fierce like a formidable wild beast; Rudra, propitiated by praise, grant happiness to him who praises (you), and let your hosts destroy him who is our adversary.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Praise the famed youth, sitting upon the high seat, the mighty one, pouncing like a terrifying wild beast.
Being praised, have mercy on the singer, Rudra. Let your weapons cast down another than us.

Keith

Praise [3] the famous youth, mounted on the chariot seat, Dread and destructive like a fierce wild beast;
Being praised, O Rudra, be merciful to the singer; Let thy missiles smite down another than us.

Griffith

Praise him the chariot-borne, the young, the famous, fierce, slaying like a dread beast of the forest.
O Rudra, praised, be gracious to the singer. let thy hosts spare us and smite down another.

Macdonell

Praise him the famed, who sits upon the car-seat The young, the fierce, like a dread beast, a slayer. When praised, be gracious, Rudra, to the singer Let thy darts pass us and lay low another.

Sing’ dem ber├╝hmten, jungen Wagenk├дmpfer, der kr├дftig angreift, wie ein grimmer L├╢we; Sei hold dem S├дnger, Rudra, du gelobter; dein Pfeil vernichte andere als wir sind.

рдкреТрд░реТрдореЗ рд╡реГреТрдХреНрд╖ рдЖрдпреБреСрдзрдиреН рдирд┐реТрдзрд╛рдпреТ

рдкрджрдкрд╛рдардГ - рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрд╛рджрд┐

рдореАрдвреБреСрд╖реНрдЯрдоред рдореАрдвреБреСрд╕реНрддреТрдореЗрддрд┐реТ рдореАрдвреБрдГреСрд╜рддрдоред рд╢рд┐рд╡реСрддреТрдореЗрддрд┐реТ рд╢рд┐рд╡реСрд╜рддрдоред рд╢рд┐реТрд╡рдГред рдирдГреТред рд╕реБреТрдордирд╛реТ рдЗрддрд┐реС рд╕реБреТрд╜рдордирд╛рдГреСред рднреТрд╡реТред рдкреТрд░реТрдореЗред рд╡реГреТрдХреНрд╖реЗред рдЖрдпреБреСрдзрдореНред рдирд┐реТрдзрд╛рдпреЗрддрд┐реС рдирд┐реТрд╜рдзрд╛рдпреСред рдХреГрддреНрддрд┐реСрдореНред рд╡рд╕рд╛реСрдирдГред рдЖред рдЪреТрд░реТред рдкрд┐рдирд╛реСрдХрдореНред рдмрд┐рднреНрд░реСрддреНред рдЖред рдЧреТрд╣рд┐реТред релрезред

рдорд╣реАрдзрд░рдГ

рдореж рдЗрдпрдореЗрдХреЛрдирд╛ рдпрд╡рдордзреНрдпрд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН рддреГрддреАрдп рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢рд╛рд░реНрдгрдГ рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░реЛрд╜рдиреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдкрд╛рджрд╛ ред рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдореАрдвреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдореАрдвреБрд╖реНрдЯрдордГ ред рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рд╢рд┐рд╡рдГ рд╢рд┐рд╡рддрдордГ ред рд╣реЗ рдореАрдвреБрд╖реНрдЯрдо рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдХрд╛рдорд╕реЗрдХреНрддрдГ, рд╣реЗ рд╢рд┐рд╡рддрдо рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдХрд░реНрддрдГ, рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рд╢рд┐рд╡рдГ рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реБрдордирд╛рдГ рд╣реГрд╖реНрдЯрдЪрд┐рддреНрддрд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдкрд░рдореЗ рджреВрд░рд╕реНрдереЗ рдЙрдиреНрдирддреЗ рд╡рд╛ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╡рдЯрд╛рджреМ рдЖрдпреБрдзрдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╢реВрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рдирд┐рдзрд╛рдп рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдерд╛рдкреНрдп рдХреГрддреНрддрд┐рдВ рдЪрд░реНрдо рд╡рд╕рд╛рдирдГ рдкрд░рд┐рджрдзрд╛рдирдГ рд╕рдиреН рдЖрдЪрд░ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫ рддрдкрд╢реНрдЪрд░реЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ ред рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрдирдкрд┐ рдкрд┐рдирд╛рдХрдВ рдзрдиреБрд░реНрдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддреН рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрд╕рдиреН рдЖрдЧрд╣рд┐ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫ ред рдЬреНрдпрд╛рд╢рд░рд╣реАрдирдВ рдзрдиреБрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рд╢реЛрдзрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрдирд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее релрез рее
рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢реАред

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рд░реБрджреНрд░рд╛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдГ
  • рдкрд░рдореЗрд╖реНрдареА рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдЛрд╖рдпрдГ
  • рдирд┐рдЪреГрджрд╛рд░реНрд╖реА рдпрд╡рдордзреНрдпрд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН
  • рдзреИрд╡рддрдГ
рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рдЯреАрдХрд╛

рдЕрде рджрд╢рдореАрдорд╛рд╣тАУ рдореАрдвреБрд╖реНрдардореЗрддрд┐ред
рдореЗ рдореАрдвреБрд╖реНрдардорд╛рддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рд╕реЗрдЪрдХ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдорднрд┐рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдХ, рд╣реЗ рд╢рд┐рд╡рддрдорд╛рддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреНрдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рд╢рд┐рд╡рдГ рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реБрдордирд╛рдГ рд╕реМрдордирд╕реНрдпреЗрди рд╕реНрдиреЗрд╣реЗрди рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡ред
рдЖрдпреБрдзрдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╢реБрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╜рддреНрдпреБрдиреНрдирддреЗ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╡рдЯрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рддреНрдерд╛рджрд┐рд░реВрдкреЗ рдирд┐рдзрд╛рдп
реирезрейрео рдпрдерд╛рд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрди рджреГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рддрдерд╛рд╜рд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкреНрдп рдХреГрддреНрддрд┐рдВ рд╡рд╕рд╛рдиреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдШреНрд░рдЪрд░реНрдордорд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рджрдзрд╛рди рдЖрдЪрд░рд╛рд╕реНрдорджрд╛рднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗрдирд╛рд╜рд╜рдЧрдЪреНрдЫред
рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрдирдкрд┐ рдкрд┐рдирд╛рдХрдВ рд╡рд┐рднреНрд░рджреНрднреВрд╖рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдзрдиреБрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рд╣рд╕реНрддреЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рдкрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрдЬреНрдпрд╛рд╜рд╜рдЧрд╣реНрдпрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫред

Keith

O most bounteous, most auspicious,
Be auspicious and favourably inclined to us;
Placing down thy weapon on the highest tree,
Clad in thy skin, come,
And approach us bearing the spear [4].

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╛рджрд┐рдХреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХреНрдпрд╛ рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ, рдпрд╣ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдореАрдвреБрд╖реНрдЯрдо) рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдордпреБрдХреНрдд (рд╢рд┐рд╡рддрдо) рдЕрддрд┐ рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдХрд╛рд░реА рд╕рднрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдХреЗ рдкрддрд┐ ! рдЖрдк (рдирдГ) рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╕реБрдордирд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрди рдЪрд┐рддреНрдд рд╕реЗ (рд╢рд┐рд╡рдГ) рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд╛рд░реА (рднрд╡) рд╣реВрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ (рдЖрдпреБрдзрдореН) рдЦрдбреНрдЧ, рднреБрд╢реБрдгреНрдбреА рдФрд░ рд╢рддрдШреНрдиреА рдЖрджрд┐ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ (рдирд┐рдзрд╛рдп) рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░ (рдХреГрддреНрддрд┐рдореН) рдореГрдЧрдЪрд░реНрдорд╛рджрд┐ рдХреА рдЕрдЩреНрдЧрд░рдЦреА рдХреЛ (рд╡рд╕рд╛рдирдГ) рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдкрд╣рд┐рдиреЗ (рдкрд┐рдирд╛рдХрдореН) рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ рдзрдиреБрд╖реН рд╡рд╛ рдмрдЦрддрд░ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЛ (рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддреН) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЖрдЧрд╣рд┐) рдЖрдЗрдпреЗ (рдкрд░рдореЗ) рдкреНрд░рдмрд▓ (рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖реЗ) рдХрд╛рдЯрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╢рддреНрд░реБ рдХреА рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдореЗрдВ (рдЖрдЪрд░) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реВрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ реерелрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╕рднрд╛ рдФрд░ рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдХреЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ рдЖрджрд┐ рд▓реЛрдЧ рдЕрдкрдиреА рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдордЩреНрдЧрд▓рд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реА рдФрд░ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреЗ рддреБрд▓реНрдп рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА рджрд╛рд╣рдХ рд╣реЛрдВ, рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рд╕рдм рд▓реЛрдЧ рдзрд░реНрдордорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдХреЛ рдЫреЛрдбрд╝ рдХреЗ рдЕрдзрд░реНрдо рдХрд╛ рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдХрднреА рди рдХрд░реЗрдВ реерелрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╕рдВ) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╕рдВ) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдореАрдвреБрд╖реНрдЯрдо рд╢рд┐рд╡рддрдо рд╕рднрд╛рд╕реЗрдиреЗрд╢ ! рддреНрд╡рдВ рдирдГ рд╕реБрдордирд╛рдГ рд╢рд┐рд╡реЛ рднрд╡ред рдЖрдпреБрдзрдВ рдирд┐рдзрд╛рдп рдХреГрддреНрддрд┐рдВ рд╡рд╕рд╛рдирдГ рдкрд┐рдирд╛рдХрдВ рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддреН рд╕рдиреНрдирд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдЧрд╣рд┐ рдкрд░рдореЗ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖ рдЖрдЪрд░ реерелрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╕рдВ) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╕рднрд╛рд╕реЗрдиреЗрд╢рд╛рджрдпрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реБ рдордЩреНрдЧрд▓рд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреЛ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯреЗрд╖реБ рдЪрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд┐рд╡ рджрд╛рд╣рдХрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдпреБрд░реНрдпреЗрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдзрд░реНрдордкрдердВ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдпрд╛рдзрд░реНрдордВ рдХрджрд╛рдкрд┐ рдирд╛рдЪрд░реЗрдпреБрдГ реерелрез рее

рднрдЯреНрдЯрднрд╛рд╕реНрдХрд░-рдЯреАрдХрд╛

рддреНрд╡рдореЗрд╡ рдкреГрдХреНрд╖рдГ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╕реНрдп рдИрд╢рд┐рд╖реЗ ред
‘рдИрд╢рд╕реНрд╕реЗ’ рдЗрддреАрдбрд╛рдЧрдордГ ред
рдкреГрдбреН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдиреНрди-рдирд╛рдо ред рдкреГрдХреНрд╖рддрд┐рд╢реН рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рдГ рдкреГрдгрдХреНрддрд┐-рдкрд░реНрдпрд╛рдпрдГ, рддрддрдГ рдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреН ред ‘рд╕рд╛рд╡реЗрдХрд╛рдЪрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддреЗрд░реБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред

рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рджрдиреНрдирд╕реНрдпреЗрд╢рд┐рд╖реЗ, рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рддреНрд╡рдореЗрд╡ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдВ рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдВ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рд╢рд░реНрдзрдГ рдмрд▓рдВ рдЪ, рддреНрд╡рджрд╛рдпрддреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ред рддреНрд╡ рд╡рд╛рддреИрд░реН рд╡рд╛рддрддреБрд▓реНрдпреИрдГ рд╡рд╛рддрдЬрд╡реИрдГ рдЕрд░реБрдгреИрдГ рд╕рдиреНрдзреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд░реНрдгреИрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реИрд░реН рдпрд╛рд╕рд┐ ред рд╢рдВрдЧрдпрдГ рд╕реБрдЦ-рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рддреНрд╡рдореЗрд╡ рдкреВрд╖рд╛ рдкреЛрд╖рдХреЛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рдзрддрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░рддрдГ рдкрд╛рд╕рд┐ рдЪрд░реБрдкреБрд░реЛрдбрд╛рд╢рд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рд╕реН рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН рдЕрд░реНрдЪрдпрддреЛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╕рд┐ ред ‘рд╢реНрд╡рдиреНрдиреБрдХреНрд╖рдиреНрдкреВрд╖рдиреН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖реБрд╖реЗрдГ рдХрдирд┐рдиреНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпреЛ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрд┐рддрдГ ред рд╡рд┐рдз рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдиреЗ рддреМрджрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдГ, ‘рд╢рддреБрд░рдиреБрдордГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддреЗрд░реБрджрд╛рддреНрдд рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рддреНрдордирд╛ рдЖрддреНрдордирд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдореЗрд╡ ред ‘рдордиреНрддреНрд░реЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рдЩреНрдпрд╛рджреЗрд░рд╛рддреНрдордирдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рд░рд▓реЛрдкрдГ ред

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд░реБрджреНрд░рд░реВрдк рдПрд╡рдВрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╕реН рддреНрд╡рдВ рд░реБрджреНрд░рддреБрд▓реНрдпрдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдореЛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрдирдпрд╛ рдШреЛрд░рдпрд╛ рддрдиреНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдорд╛рд░рдпреЗрддрд┐ рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред ‘рдПрд╖рд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдШреЛрд░рд╛ рддрдиреВрд░реНрдпрджреНрд░реНрджреНрд░рдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, are Rudra, the expeller (of foes) from the expanse of heaven; you are the strength of the Maruts; you are supreme over (sacrificial) food; you, who are plural asantly domiciled (in the hall of sacrifice), go with ruddy horses, (fleet as) the wind; as P┼лс╣гan, you cherish, of yours own will, those who offer worship.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, as lord of great heaven, are Rudra; you, as the troop of Maruts, are master of strengthening nourishment [=rain].
You, as luck for livestock, drive with the ruddy winds (as horses); you, as P┼лс╣гan, protect the ones doing honor, in your own person.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand the cmpd ┼Ыaс╣Гgay├б-. Wackernagel (AIG II.1.309) classifies it with cmpds with governing first-member prepositions, but ┼Ы├бm, though uninflected, does not function like even the improper prepositions/preverbs like ├бram. He does recognize its singularity (314-15), but keeps it in this category, in which it seems out of place.

Griffith

Rudra art thou, the Asura of mighty heaven: thou art the Maruts’ host, thou art the Lord of food,
Thou goest with red winds: bliss hast thou in thine home. As Pusan thou thyself protectest worshippers.

Oldenberg

Thou, O Agni, art Rudra, the Asura of the high Heaven 1;
thou, being the host of the Maruts, rulest over nourishment.
Thou goest along with the flame-coloured Winds, bringing happiness to our home.
Thou, being P├╗shan, protectest thy worshippers by thy own might.

Keith

Thou, O Agni, art Rudra, the Asura of the mighty sky,
Thou art the host of the Maruts, thou art lord of food;
Thou farest with ruddy winds, blessing the household;
Thou, as Pusan dost, protectest thy worshippers with thyself.

Geldner

Du, Agni, bist Rudra, der Asura des gro├Яen Himmels; als Marutheer verf├╝gst du ├╝ber die St├дrke. Du f├дhrst mit den r├╢tlichen Windrossen, dem Hausstand heilbringend; du sch├╝tzest als Pusan in eigener Person die Verehrer.

Grassmann

Und Rudra bist du, des erhabnen Himmels Geist, die Marutschar, o Agni, Labung wohnt dir bei; Auf feur’gen Winden gehst du, bringst uns Gl├╝ck ins Haus, und Puschan bist du, sch├╝tzest die Verehrer recht.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSecure Agni, the king of sacrifice, the afflicter (of foes), the invoker (of the gods), the distributor of food through heaven and earth, the golden-formed, for your protection before (surprised by) sudden death.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Pur─Б tanayitnor acitt─Бt = liс╣н, before the unconsciousness of the thunderbolt; this implies a state of unconsciousness, or death as sudden as if the work of the thunderbolt

Jamison Brereton

Make [=ignite] him here, the king, the Rudra of your ceremony, the Hotar whose sacrifice comes true in the two world-halves,
Agni of golden formтАФ(make him) for help for you in the face of
unexpected thundering.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I render vs.-final kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam twice – once with vs.-initial ─Б╠Бin the meaning тАШmake = kindleтАЩ, rather than with most tr. тАШbring hereтАЩ, and once with the quasiinfinitival dat. ├бvase.

It is not entirely clear why Agni is identified as Rudra here. The word is most likely to be construed with the gen. adhvar├бsya as тАЬthe Rudra of the/your ceremony,тАЭ on the basis of I.114.4 rudr├бс╣Г yaj├▒as─Б╠Бdham тАЬRudra bringing the sacrifice to successтАЭ and III.2.5 (also of Agni) rudr├бс╣Г yaj├▒─Б╠Бn─Бс╣Г s─Б╠Бdhadiс╣гс╣нim тАЬthe Rudra of the sacrifices, bringing success to the offerings.тАЭ Perhaps the point of comparison is RudraтАЩs healing powers and, esp. here, his ability to ward off threats of all sorts, in this case the тАЬunexpected thunderingтАЭ (tanayitn├│r ac├нtt─Бt) of p─Бda c.

r├│dasyoс╕е can be either gen. (with most tr.) or loc. (so published translation). There is little riding on the choice.

As most interpr. take it, тАЬunexpected thunderingтАЭ is probably a reference to all sorts of unforeseen dangers, rather than specifically of a sudden storm.

Griffith

WIN, to assist you, Rudra, Lord of worship, Priest of both worlds, effectual
Sacrificer,
Agni, invested with his golden colours, before the thunder strike and lay you senseless.

Oldenberg

Draw Rudra hither for your protection 1, the king of sacrifice, the truly sacrificing Hotri of the two worlds 2, the golden-coloured Agni, before the unseen thunderbolt (strikes you).

Geldner

Den K├╢nig eures Opfers, den Rudra, den wahrhaft opfernden Hotri beider Welten, den goldfarbigen Agni gewinnet zur Gunst, noch rechtzeitg vor dem unerwarteten Donnerschlag.

Grassmann

Des Opfers K├╢nig, ihn den hehren Agni, der recht verehrt, den Priester beider Welten, Eh’ noch der laute Donnerer gewahrt wird, schafft euch zur H├╝lfe her, den goldgef├дrbten.

Elizarenkova

рдореж рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрд░реБрдХреНрдордордзрдГрдкрд┐рдгреНрдбрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдорд┐рддрд┐’ (рдХрд╛. резрен ред рей ред реиреп)ред ‘рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ’ (рдкрд╛реж резредрекред реореи) рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрд╛рдгрд┐рдирд┐рд╕реНрдорд░рдгрд╛рддреН ред рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдмреГрд╣рддреН рд░реБрдХреНрдорд░реВрдкреЛрд╜рдпрдорд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрдГ рд╕реАрдорддрдГ рд╕реАрдорд╛рдирдВ рдорд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд╛рдВ рднреВрдЧреЛрд▓рдордзреНрдпрднрд╛рдЧрдорд╛рд░рднреНрдп рд╕реБрд░реБрдЪрдГ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рд░реЛрдЪрдиреНрддреЗ рд╢реЛрднрдиреНрддреЗ рддрд╛рдиреН рд╕реБрд░реЛрдЪрдирд╛рдирд┐рдорд╛рдиреН рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐ рдЖрд╡рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╡реГрддрд╛рдирдХрд░реЛрддреНрд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗрди ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо ред рдкреНрд░рдердордорд╛рджреМ рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреНрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВ рджрд┐рд╢рд┐ рдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдЬрд╛рдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдорд╛рдирдореН ред рдЬрдиреЗрдГ рд╢рд╛рдирдЪрд┐ рд╢рдкрдГ рд╢реНрд▓реМ рд╕рддрд┐ рдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдорд┐рддрд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рд╡реЗрдирдГ рдХрд╛рдордиреАрдпреЛ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡реА рд╡рд╛ рд╕ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрдГ рдмреБрдзреНрдиреНрдпрд╛ рдмреБрдзреНрдирдордиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдВ рддрддреНрд░ рднрд╡рд╛ рдмреБрдзреНрдиреНрдпрд╛ рджрд┐рд╢рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╡рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╡реГрдгреЛрддрд┐ ред рд╕рддреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╡рдГ ред рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрддрд┐ ред рд╡реГрдгреЛрддреЗрдГ рд╢рдкрд┐ рд▓реБрдкреНрддреЗ рд▓рдЩрд┐ рдЧреБрдгреЗ рдЪ рд╡ рдЗрддрд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдЕрдбрднрд╛рд╡ рдЖрд░реНрд╖рдГ ред ‘рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпрдорд╛рдЩрдпреЛрдЧреЗрд╜рдкрд┐’ (рдкрд╛реж рем ред рек ред ренрел) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рддреН ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢реАрд░реНрдмреБрдзреНрдиреНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рдЬрдЧрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрд╕реНрдерд╛рдирднреВрддрд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдВ рддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╕реБ рддрд╛рдГ ред ‘рдЕрдореНрдмрд╛рдореНрдмрдЧреЛрднреВрдорд┐-’ (рдкрд╛реж реоредрей ред репрен) рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рд╖рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдп рдПрд╡ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдиреН рджрд┐рд╢реЛ рднреВрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдЪрд╛рднрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдирдХреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ реерейрее
рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереАред

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпреЛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛
  • рд╡рддреНрд╕рд╛рд░ рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ
  • рдирд┐рдЪреГрддреНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН
  • рдзреИрд╡рддрдГ
рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХрд┐рд╕ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛ рдХреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ рее

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдЯреАрдХрд╛

рдпрджреЗрддрдЬреНрдЬрдЧрддреНрдХрд╛рд░рдгрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо ‘рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдордирдиреНрддрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╢реНрд░реБрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рддрджреЗрддрддреН рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрд╛рджреМ рдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдЬрдЧрджрд╛рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдгреЛрддреНрдкрджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╕рддреН рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреН рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВ рджрд┐рд╢рд┐ рд╡реЗрдирдГ рдХрдордиреАрдп рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпреЛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрд░реБрдЪрдГ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕реАрдорддрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрдкрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдореЛрджрдЧреНрджрд┐рдЧреНрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╕реАрдореНрдиреЛ рд╡рд┐рднрдЬреНрдп рдЖрд╡рдГ рдЖрд╡реГрдгреЛрддреН ред рд╕ рд╡реЗрдирдГ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпреЛ рдмреБрдзреНрдирд┐рдпрд╛рдГ рдмреБрдзреНрдирдВ рдореВрд▓рдВ рддрддреНрд░ рднрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢рд╡рд╛рдпреНрд╡рдЧреНрдирд┐рдЬрд▓рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрдГ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рднрдЬреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╛ рдЕрдХрд░реЛрджрд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╕рддрд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдЧрд┐рд░рд┐рдирджреАрд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рджреЗрдГ рдЕрд╕рддрд╢реНрдЪ рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдпреЛрдирд┐рдВ рдХрд╛рд░рдгрдВ рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрдВ рднреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рд░реВрдкрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╡рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╡реГрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдЬрдЧрджреНрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдВ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ (рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреН) рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХреА рдЖрджрд┐ рдореЗрдВ (рдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН) рд╕рдм рдХрд╛ рдЙрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдХ рдФрд░ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд╛ (рдкреНрд░рдердордореН) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдХрд░реНрддрд╛ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рд╕рдм рд╕реЗ рдмрдбрд╝рд╛ рдЬреЛ (рд╕реБрд░реБрдЪрдГ) рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рд░реБрдЪрд┐ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп (рд╡реЗрдирдГ) рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдЬрд┐рд╕ (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рдЗрд╕ рдХреЗ (рдмреБрдзреНрдиреНрдпрд╛рдГ) рдЬрд▓ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзреА рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рди рд╕реВрд░реНрдп, рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛, рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдФрд░ рдирдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░ рдЖрджрд┐ (рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдз рд╕реНрдерд▓реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╕реНрдерд┐рдд (рдЙрдкрдорд╛рдГ) рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЗ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрдд рд▓реЛрдХ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЙрди рд╕рдм рдХреЛ (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╣ (рдЖрд╡рдГ) рдЕрдкрдиреА рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдЖрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрди рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ (рд╡рд┐рд╕реАрдорддрдГ) рдорд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рджрд╛ рд╕реЗ (рд╕рддрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рди рджреЗрдЦрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рдЪ) рдФрд░ (рдЕрд╕рддрдГ) рдЕрд╡реНрдпрдХреНрдд (рдЪ) рдФрд░ рдХрд╛рд░рдг рдХреЗ (рдпреЛрдирд┐рдореН) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢рд░реВрдк рд╕реНрдерд╛рди рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐рд╡рдГ) рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕реА рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдХреА рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛ рд╕рдм рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдирд┐рддреНрдп рдЕрд╡рд╢реНрдп рдХрд░рдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерей рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬEarnetly I glorify the exploits of Viс╣гс╣Зu, who made the three worlds; who sustained the lofty aggregate site (of the spheres); thrice traversing (the whole); who is praised by the exalted.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

P─Бrthiv─Бni vimame raj─Бс╣Гsi = lit. he made the earthly regions;

Pс╣Ыthiv─л = three worlds: atra trayo lok─Б api pс╣Ыthiv─л ┼Ыabdav─Бcy─Б; Indra and Agni are said to abide in the lower, middle and upper pс╣Ыthiv─л or world– yad indr─Бgn─л avamasy─Бm pс╣Ыth─лvy─Бm madhyamasy─Бm paramasyam uta stha (RV. 1.108.9; Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 1.2.12.1); seven lower lok─Бs are also included in the word pс╣Ыthiv─л;or, the term is limited to the three regions addressed in prayer, bh┼лс╕е bhuvar svar; who sustained the lofty: uttaram sadhastham askabh─Бyat: sadastha = the firmament, as the asylum of the three regions– lokatray─Б┼Ыrayabh┼лtam antarikс╣гam; or, the seven regions above the earth; or, the highest region of all, whence there is no return; or the above of the righteous, the satya-loka;

Askabh─Бyat = nirmitav─Бn, created; thrice traversing: vicakram─Бс╣Зas tredh─Б (idam viс╣гс╣Зurvi cakrame: RV. 1.22.17); traversing in various ways in own created worlds

Jamison Brereton

Now shall I proclaim the heroic deeds of Viс╣гс╣Зu, who measured out the earthly realms,
who propped up the higher seat, having stridden out three times, the wide-ranging one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hymn begins with an almost exact echo of the famous opening p─Бda of the Indra hymn I.32 ├нndrasya n├║ v─лry─Б╠Ас╣Зi pr├б vocam. In place of ├нndrasya we have v├нс╣гс╣Зoс╕е and the missing syllable is made up by inserting the fairly functionless particle kam after n├║.

Griffith

I WILL declare the mighty deeds of Visnu, of him who measured out the earthly regions,
Who propped the highest place of congregation, thrice setting down his footstep, widely striding.

Macdonell

I will proclaim the mighty deeds of Viс╣гс╣Зu, Of him who measured out the earthly spaces; Who, firmly propping up the higher station, Strode out in triple regions, widely pacing.

Keith

I shall proclaim the mighty deeds of Visnu
Who meted out the spaces of the earth,
Who established the highest abode,
Stepping thrice, the far-goer.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay I attain his favourite path, in which god-seeking men delight; (the path) of that wide-stepping Viс╣гс╣Зu, in whose exalted station there is a (perpetual) flow of felicity; for to such a degree is he the friend (of the pious).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

His favourite path: the firmament: patho anatarikс╣гam

Jamison Brereton

Might I reach that dear cattle-pen of his, where men seeking the gods find elation,
for exactly that is the bond to the wide-striding one: the wellspring of honey in the highest step of Viс╣гс╣Зu.

Griffith

May I attain to that his well-loved mansion where men devoted to the Gods are happy.
For there springs, close akin to the Wide-Strider, the well of meath in Visnu’s highest footstep.

Macdonell

I would attain to that his dear dominion Where men devoted to the gods do revel. In the wide-striding Viс╣гс╣Зu’s highest footstep There is a spring of mead: such is our kinship.

Geldner

An seinen lieben Zufluchtsort m├╢chte ich gelangen, an dem die gottergebenen M├дnner schwelgen, denn dort ist diese Genossenschaft des Weitschreitenden. In der h├╢chsten Fu├Яspur des Vishnu ist der Quell des Honigs.

Grassmann

O m├╢cht’ ich seinen lieben Sitz erreichen, in dem die frommen M├дnner selig leben; Denn das sind recht des m├дcht’gen Schreiters Freunde, und S├╝sses quillt an Vischnu’s h├╢chster Fussspur.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬViс╣гс╣Зu is therefore glorified, that by his prowess he is like a fearful, ravenous, and mountain-haunting wild beast, and because of that in his three paces all worlds abide.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mountain-haunting wild beast: mс╣Ыga or siс╣Гha, a lion, as applicable to Viс╣гс╣Зu: one who seeks for his enemies to inflict punishment on them, and is therefore, fearful and fierce;

Giriс╣гс╣нh─Бс╕е = he who dwells on high, or who abides in prayer and the like: mantr─Бdir┼лp─Бy─Бm v─Бci artam─Бnaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

In this way Viс╣гс╣Зu will be praised for his heroic deedтАФ(he who is) like a fearsome wild beast, living in the mountains and roaming wherever it wants,
in whose three wide strides dwell all living beings.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The covert identification with Indra continues in p─Бda b, which is identical to X.180.2a, where Indra is the referent.

Griffith

For this his mighty deed is Visnu lauded, like some wild beast, dread, prowling, mountain-roaming;
He within whose three wide-extended paces all living creatures have their habitation.

Macdonell

Because of this his mighty deed is Viс╣гс╣Зu Lauded, like some fierce beast that is much dreaded, That wanders as it lists, that haunts the mountains: He in whose three wide strides abide all creatures.

Geldner

Also wird Vishnu ob seiner Heldentat gepriesen, der umherschweifend im Gebirge haust wie das furchtbare wilde Tier, in dessen drei weiten Schritten alle Gesch├╢pfe Wohnung finden.

Grassmann

Ger├╝hmt wird Vischnu wegen dieser Grossthat, gleich wildem L├╢wen, der durch Berge schweifet, Er, unter dessen drei gewalt’gen Schritten die Wesen alle sichre Wohnung haben.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬExpanding with a body beyond all measure, Viс╣гс╣Зu men comprehend not your magnitude; we knowthese your two worlds (computing) from the earth, but you, divine Viс╣гс╣Зu, are cognisant of the highest.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Your twoworlds: i.e. the earth and the firmament, which are visible; cf. RV. 10.082.05

Jamison Brereton

O you who have grown with your body beyond measure, they do not attain to your greatness.
We (only) know both your dusky realms of the earth; god Viс╣гс╣Зu, you yourself know the farthest one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Renou supplies тАЬother godsтАЭ as the subj. of ├бnv a┼Ыnuvanti in b. This seems perfectly acceptable, though not strictly necessary. And since in vs. 2 it is, presumably, mortals (since they are тАШbornтАЩ) who fail to reach the limit of Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs greatness, mortals could also be the subject here. See remarks below on the formulatic connection between the two vss.

As Renou points out, both the case of the complement (acc. versus gen.) and the voice (act. versus mid.) differ between 1st pl. vidma in c and 2nd sg. vitse in d. The middle voice of vitse makes sense, since Viс╣гс╣Зu knows his own farthest realm; the variation in case is harder to account for. Perhaps the two earthly realms are subjects of direct knowledge, while the farthest realm is something even Viс╣гс╣Зu only knows of.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The b-p─Бdas of these two vss. are variants of each other, using two different roots for тАШattainтАЩ (тИЪna┼Ы, тИЪ─Бp) and two different formulations of тАШgreatnessтАЩ, the 2nd an elaboration on the first: 1b n├б te mahitv├бm ├бnv a┼Ыnuvanti 2ab n├б te тАж mahimn├бс╕е p├бram ├бntam ─Бpa Another example of the freedom of RVic formulaics; see comm. ad VII.98.5 in the previous hymn for further on this.

Griffith

MEN come not nigh thy majesty who growest beyond all bound and measure with thy body.
Both thy two regions of the earth, O Visnu, we know: thou God, knowest the highest also.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis Viс╣гс╣Зu traversed the earth for a dwelling which he was desirous of giving to his eulogist; firm arethe people who are his praisers; he who is the engenderer of good has made a spacious dwelling (for hisworshippers).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Which he was desirous of giving: manuс╣гe da┼Ыasyan = stuvate devagaс╣З─Бya, to the company ofgods praising him– Viс╣гс╣Зu having taken the three worlds from the Asuras to give to them; the engenderer ofgood: or, to whom belong fortunate births

Jamison Brereton

Quick Viс╣гс╣Зu strode across this earth for a dwelling place for Manu, showing his favor.
Firmly fixed are his peoples, (even) the weak. He, affording good birth, has made (them) wide dwelling.

Jamison Brereton Notes

By concentrating Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs strides in the first p─Бda of 4, the poet is free to express the aim of Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs action – creating space and dwelling places for the people

– in the rest of the vs. As Geldner points out (n. 4c), asya can refer either to Viс╣гс╣Зu or to Manu, although in actuality this may not matter. It may be an instance of тАЬtrickle-downтАЭ ownership: Viс╣гс╣Зu makes a dwelling place for Manu, and in turn ManuтАЩs people also get firmly planted. Or, Manu and the people may both be under Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs auspices.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, vss. 3 and 4 are responsive. The first p─Бda of 4 concentrates the essence of the 1st two p─Бdas of 3, substituting v├н cakrame (of 3b) for tr├нr dev├бс╕е (in 3a) at the beginning of the p─Бda. This phrase, tr├нr dev├бс╕е, is short a syllable; Oldenberg suggests reading t╬Зrir, but this seems unlikely: I donтАЩt know of any other disyllabic readings of this extremely common numeral (either as 1st cmpd member tri- or adverbial tr├нs). I suggest rather that the metrically disturbed opening draws attention to the beginning of this set of paired vss. by being flawed and is тАЬrepairedтАЭ by 4a. See similar remarks about 3c and 5c ad vs. 5.

Griffith

Over this earth with mighty step strode Visnu, ready to give it for a home to Manu.
In him the humble people trust for safety: he, nobly born, hath made them spacious dwellings.

English translation:

Jamison Brereton

Three times did the quick god stride with his greatness across this earth worth a hundred verses.
Let Viс╣гс╣Зu be preeminent, stronger than the strong, for vibrant is the
name of this stalwart one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Flg. a suggestion by Geldner (n. 3a, though not reflected in his tr.), I take eс╣г├бin p─Бda a (also 4a) as belonging to the stem eс╣г├б- тАШquickтАЩ, which is used several times of Viс╣гс╣Зu in the gen. expression v├нс╣гс╣Зor eс╣г├бsya (II.34.11, VII.40.5, VIII.20.3), in which confusion with the nom. pronominal eс╣г├б(с╕е) (possible here) is excluded.

The hapax ┼Ыat├бrcas- is problematic. The Pp analyses the 2nd member as arcasam, but Wackernagel (AiG I.318) points out that the sandhi between the cmpd members would require rather -с╣Ыcasam. However, Oldenberg disputes this, claiming that it would then have to be written (тАЬтАж geschrieben werden m├╝ssenтАЭ) *┼Ыat├бс╣Ыcasam , though itтАЩs not clear to me why. Interpr. differ significantly: S─Бyaс╣Зa. glosses with arcis-.

Oldenberg posits a masc. s-stem *arc├бs- тАШsingerтАЩ, comparing VI.34.3 y├бdi stot─Б╠Бraс╕е ┼Ыat├бс╣Г y├бt sah├бsraс╣Г gс╣Ыс╣З├бnti тАЬWhen a hundred, when a thousand praisers sing to him тАж,тАЭ an interpr. followed by Geldner – though the connection between the two passages seems tenuous to me. By contrast, Renou tr. тАЬau cent ├йclats,тАЭ perhaps flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs arc├нs-. Since an infinitival dat. с╣Ыc├бse тАШto praise, for chanting (praise)тАЩ is found in VI.39.5 and VII.61.6, it seems reasonable to take the underlying stem с╣Ыcas- as the base here, as Grassmann does, glossing тАШhundertfach zu preisenтАЩ. My тАШworth a hundred versesтАЩ is close to that, though perhaps тАШpraises, chantsтАЩ would be better.

Because of the lack of accent on asya, it should be pronominal, not adjectival; I would adjust the tr. to тАЬof him, the stalwart.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, vss. 3 and 4 are responsive. The first p─Бda of 4 concentrates the essence of the 1st two p─Бdas of 3, substituting v├н cakrame (of 3b) for tr├нr dev├бс╕е (in 3a) at the beginning of the p─Бda. This phrase, tr├нr dev├бс╕е, is short a syllable; Oldenberg suggests reading t╬Зrir, but this seems unlikely: I donтАЩt know of any other disyllabic readings of this extremely common numeral (either as 1st cmpd member tri- or adverbial tr├нs). I suggest rather that the metrically disturbed opening draws attention to the beginning of this set of paired vss. by being flawed and is тАЬrepairedтАЭ by 4a. See similar remarks about 3c and 5c ad vs. 5.

рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН

+режрем рд╢реНрд░реА-рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ...{Loading}...
рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН-рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрдпрдГ

The celebrated shrI sUkta has spread widely beyond its original role in the vedic gR^ihya liturgy and prayoga-s of the vedic vidhAna-s. Its earliest occurrences are seen in the khila of the R^igveda and the bodhAyana and vaikhAnasa mantra pATha-s of the kR^iShNa yajur veda. It is also related to the ShaShThI sUkta of the mAnava gR^ihya sUtra. The tantric literature also mentions itтАФthe most prominent mention is in the lakShmI tantra (LT 36.121-140 and LT 50.1-237). LT50.1-2367 gives a detailed account of the pAncharatric prayoga of the shrI sUkta in worshiping lakShmI. The lakShmI-ratna kosha is another text providing its deployment in the worship of shrI. In the kAdividyA stream of shrI-kula tradition a saMpuTikaraNa of the sUkta and the panchadashI (and other bIja-s like mAya, shrI, kAma, vANI and tripurashekharAnta) is a favored mode of deployment. The shrI sUkta has even been retained by the bauddha nAstika-s and this tradition was until recently alive in Nepal and Bhutan.

The pure vedic form of both the yajurvedic and R^igvedic traditions are no longer commonly practiced, especially in South India. Instead, what one has is a vulgate that is widely used in the drAviDa, Andhra and karnATa countries. It may be recited in a pseudo-yajurvedic form without following the rules of yajurvedic phonetics (e.g. hirANyavarNAM harinIM suvarNa тАж instead of the correct yajuSh form: hirANyavarNA{\m+} harinI{\m+} suvarNa тАж as is specified, for example, in the bodhAyana mantra pATha) or in a form typical of R^igvedic recitation.

Original R^ivedic version is often termed the kAshmIra-pATha because it appears to have been retained in those regions.
